**Candidate 26:** `T*c0*epsilon² + c1*epsilon*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*epsilon² + c4*epsilon*(T+c5)^c6`

Set c6=1: c4*epsilon*(T+c5) = c4*epsilon*T + c4*c5*epsilon. Then total: T*(c0*epsilon² + c4*epsilon) + c1*epsilon*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*epsilon² + c4*c5*epsilon. Has exp and epsilon²*T terms. Set c0=0, c1=0: T*c4*epsilon + c3*epsilon² + c4*c5*epsilon. Missing T²*epsilon.

**Candidate 26 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 29:** `T*c0*epsilon^c1 + c2*epsilon^c3 + c4*epsilon*(T+c5)^c6`

**Candidate 108:** `T²*c0*epsilon^c1 + T*c2*epsilon² + c3*epsilon*exp(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon²`

**Candidate 70:** `T²*c0 + T*c1*epsilon^c2 + c3*epsilon^c4 + c5`

**Candidate 26:** `T*c0*epsilon² + c1*epsilon*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3*epsilon² + c4*epsilon*(T+c5)^c6`

Set c6=2, c0=0, c1=0, c3=0: c4*epsilon*(T+c5)² = epsilon*(c4*T² + 2c4*c5*T + c4*c5²). This works! ✓

But wait - can we also keep c0 and c3? With c6=2, c1=0:
T*c0*epsilon² + c3*epsilon² + c4*epsilon*(T²+2c5*T+c5²)
= c4*epsilon*T² + (c0*epsilon² + 2c4*c5*epsilon)*T + c3*epsilon² + c4*c5²*epsilon

The T term has both epsilon² and epsilon components: (c0*epsilon² + 2c4*c5*epsilon)*T. For this to equal B*epsilon*T, we need c0=0. Then: c4*epsilon*T² + 2c4*c5*epsilon*T + c3*epsilon² + c4*c5²*epsilon. Need c3=0 for pure epsilon form. Then: epsilon*(c4*T² + 2c4*c5*T + c4*c5²). ✓ MATCH confirmed.
